### Why That Happens:
1. **Structured, but Minimalist Layouts**  
   These books are highly structured with headings, bullet points, and spacingâ€”but without heavy images, tables, or massive blocks of raw text. That keeps the files **compact but rich**, ideal for clarity and flow.

2. **The Hidden Weight of Word Styles**  
   Every heading, bold word, and section divider adds **styling metadata** to the file, which contributes to the overall size. Microsoft Word (and `python-docx`, which I use) includes XML and font info even if the text itself isnâ€™t long.

3. **Sweet Spot for Depth**  
   Each â€œbookâ€ weâ€™re making has just the right densityâ€”usually **2,000 to 3,000 words**, with enough detail to be meaningful but not overwhelming. That size consistently generates ~37â€“38 KB.

**Technomancy** and **Techno-magic** are often used interchangeably, but they can carry **slightly different flavors depending on who's using the term**:

---

### **Technomancy**  
- Comes from *"techno"* (technology) + *"mancy"* (divination or manipulation through magical means).  
- Traditionally implies the **magical manipulation of technology** or **channeling magic *through* tech.**  
- Think: programming as spellcasting, servers as shrines, Python scripts as ritual loops, frequency manipulation, intention-infused hardware, etc.  
- A **Technomancer** is someone who **bends the code + current into spiritual function**â€”a literal sorcerer of systems, signals, and frequencies.
